      <p><b>Nova Scotia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/?/: secondary stress follows">?</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/o?/: 'o' in 'code'">o?</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/?/: 'a' in 'about'">?</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/?/: primary stress follows">?</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/o?/: 'o' in 'code'">o?</span><span title="/?/: 'sh' in 'shy'">?</span><span title="/?/: 'a' in 'about'">?</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">NOH</span>-v? <span style="font-size:90%">SKOH</span>-sh?</i></a>) (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scottish Gaelic</a>: <i lang="gd">Alba Nuadh</i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Nouvelle-Écosse</i>) is one of the thirteen <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">provinces and territories</a> of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. It is one of the three <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime Canada">Maritime provinces</a> and one of the four <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic provinces</a>. Nova Scotia is <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for "New Scotland". Most of the population are <a href="/wiki/Native_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Native language">native</a> English-speakers. </p>
      <p>With a population of 923,598 as of 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-2016census_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016census-2">[2]</a></sup> it is the most populous of Canada's four <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic provinces</a>. It is the country's <a href="/wiki/Population_of_Canada_by_province_and_territory" title="Population of Canada by province and territory">second-most densely populated</a> province and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_area" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by area">second-smallest</a> province by area, both after neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2016census_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016census-2">[2]</a></sup> Its area of 55,284 square kilometres (21,345&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) includes <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a> and 3,800 other coastal islands. The <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_peninsula" title="Nova Scotia peninsula">peninsula</a> that makes up Nova Scotia's <a href="/wiki/Mainland" title="Mainland">mainland</a> is connected to the rest of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Chignecto" title="Isthmus of Chignecto">Isthmus of Chignecto</a>, on which the province's land border with <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> is located. The province borders the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a> to the west and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the south and east, and is separated from Prince Edward Island and the island of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Strait" title="Northumberland Strait">Northumberland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cabot_Strait" title="Cabot Strait">Cabot</a> straits, respectively. </p>
      <p>The land that comprises what is now Nova Scotia has been inhabited by the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Mi%EA%9E%8Ckmaq" title="Mi?kmaq">Mi?kmaq</a> people for thousands of years. In 1605, <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>'s first <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> colony, was founded with the creation of Acadia's capital, <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Port-Royal_National_Historic_Site" title="Port-Royal National Historic Site">Port-Royal</a></span>. Britain fought France for the territory on numerous occasions for over a century afterwards. The <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Louisbourg" title="Fortress of Louisbourg">Fortress of Louisbourg</a> was a key focus point in the battle for control. Following the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Acadians" title="Expulsion of the Acadians">Great Upheaval</a> (1755-1763) where the British deported the <a href="/wiki/Acadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Acadian">Acadians</a> en masse, the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_New_France_(1758%E2%80%931760)" title="Conquest of New France (1758–1760)">Conquest of New France</a> (1758-1760) by the British, and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a> (1763), France had to surrender Acadia to the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> (1775-1783), thousands of <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalists</a> settled in Nova Scotia. In 1848, Nova Scotia became the first British colony to achieve <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a>, and it <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">federated</a> in July 1867 with New Brunswick and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>) to form what is now the country of Canada. </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia's <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a>, which today is home to about 45 percent of the province's population. Halifax is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_census_metropolitan_areas_and_agglomerations_in_Canada" title="List of census metropolitan areas and agglomerations in Canada">thirteenth-largest</a> census metropolitan area in Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> the largest city in Atlantic Canada, and Canada's second-largest coastal city after <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Etymology_of_Scotland" title="Etymology of Scotland">Etymology of Scotland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>"Nova Scotia" means "New <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and is the recognized <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English-language</a> name for the province. In both French and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>, the province is directly translated as "New Scotland" (French: <i><i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Nouvelle-Écosse</i></i>. Gaelic: <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic-language text">Alba Nuadh</i></i>). In general, Romance and Slavic languages use a direct translation of "New Scotland", while most other languages use direct transliterations of the Latin / English name. </p>
      <p>The province was first named in the 1621 Royal Charter granting to <a href="/wiki/William_Alexander,_1st_Earl_of_Stirling" title="William Alexander, 1st Earl of Stirling">Sir William Alexander</a> in 1632 the right to settle lands including modern Nova Scotia, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gasp%C3%A9_Peninsula" title="Gaspé Peninsula">Gaspé Peninsula</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-royalcharter_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royalcharter-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Geography of Nova Scotia">Geography of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_provincial_parks_in_Nova_Scotia" title="List of provincial parks in Nova Scotia">List of provincial parks in Nova Scotia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Nova_Scotia" title="List of protected areas of Nova Scotia">List of protected areas of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia is Canada's second-smallest province in area, after <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>. The province's mainland is the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_peninsula" title="Nova Scotia peninsula">Nova Scotia peninsula</a>, surrounded by the Atlantic Ocean and including numerous bays and estuaries. Nowhere in Nova Scotia is more than 67&nbsp;km (42&nbsp;mi) from the ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a>, a large island to the northeast of the Nova Scotia mainland, is also part of the province, as is <a href="/wiki/Sable_Island" title="Sable Island">Sable Island</a>, a small island notorious for being the site of offshore shipwrecks,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> approximately 175&nbsp;km (110&nbsp;mi) from the province's southern coast. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Novascotia_topo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Novascotia_topo.png/220px-Novascotia_topo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Novascotia_topo.png/330px-Novascotia_topo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Novascotia_topo.png/440px-Novascotia_topo.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1596"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Novascotia_topo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topographic map of Nova Scotia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia has many ancient fossil-bearing rock formations. These formations are particularly rich on the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a>'s shores. Blue Beach near <a href="/wiki/Hantsport" title="Hantsport">Hantsport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joggins_Fossil_Cliffs" class="mw-redirect" title="Joggins Fossil Cliffs">Joggins Fossil Cliffs</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a>'s shores, has yielded an abundance of <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a>-age fossils. Wasson's Bluff, near the town of <a href="/wiki/Parrsboro" title="Parrsboro">Parrsboro</a>, has yielded both <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a>- and <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a>-age fossils. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/White_Hill_(Nova_Scotia)" title="White Hill (Nova Scotia)">White Hill</a> at 533m (1,749&nbsp;ft) above sea level, situated amongst the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Highlands" title="Cape Breton Highlands">Cape Breton Highlands</a> in the far north of the province. </p>
      <p>The province contains 5,400 lakes.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nova_Scotia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nova_Scotia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/220px-Nova_Scotia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nova_Scotia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/330px-Nova_Scotia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Nova_Scotia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/440px-Nova_Scotia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="945"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nova_Scotia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> of Nova Scotia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Climate of Nova Scotia">Climate of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia lies in the mid-temperate zone and, although the province is almost surrounded by water, the climate is closer to <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a> rather than <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime</a>. The winter and summer temperature extremes of the continental climate are moderated by the ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-ECclimate_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECclimate-14">[14]</a></sup> However, winters are cold enough to be classified as continental—still being nearer the freezing point than inland areas to the west. The Nova Scotian climate is in many ways similar to the central <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> coast in Northern Europe, only wetter and snowier. This is true although Nova Scotia is some fifteen parallels further south. Areas not on the Atlantic coast experience warmer summers more typical of inland areas, and winter lows are a little colder. On 12 August 2020, the community of Grand Étang, famous for its <a href="/wiki/Suetes" title="Suetes">Les Suêtes</a> winds recorded a balmy overnight low of 23.3 Celsius<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Described on the provincial vehicle licence plate as Canada's Ocean Playground, Nova Scotia is surrounded by four major bodies of water: the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">Gulf of Saint Lawrence</a> to the north, the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a> to the west, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Maine" title="Gulf of Maine">Gulf of Maine</a> to the southwest, and the Atlantic Ocean to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-ECclimate_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECclimate-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Nova_Scotia" title="History of Nova Scotia">History of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Military history of Nova Scotia">Military history of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mi%27kmaq_people_at_Tufts_Cove,_Nova_Scotia,_Canada,_ca._1871.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mi%27kmaq_people_at_Tufts_Cove%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_ca._1871.jpg/220px-Mi%27kmaq_people_at_Tufts_Cove%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_ca._1871.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mi%27kmaq_people_at_Tufts_Cove%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_ca._1871.jpg/330px-Mi%27kmaq_people_at_Tufts_Cove%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_ca._1871.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Mi%27kmaq_people_at_Tufts_Cove%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_ca._1871.jpg/440px-Mi%27kmaq_people_at_Tufts_Cove%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_ca._1871.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2945" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mi%27kmaq_people_at_Tufts_Cove,_Nova_Scotia,_Canada,_ca._1871.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mi%27kmaq" class="mw-redirect" title="Mi'kmaq">Mi'kmaq</a> family in <a href="/wiki/Tuft%27s_Cove,_Nova_Scotia" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuft's Cove, Nova Scotia">Tuft's Cove</a>, 1871. The Mi'kmaq inhabited Nova Scotia when the first Europeans arrived.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The province includes regions of the <a href="/wiki/Mi%27kmaq_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Mi'kmaq people">Mi'kmaq</a> nation of Mi'kma'ki (<i><i lang="mic" title="Mi'kmaq-language text">mi'gama'gi</i></i>). (The territory of the Nation of Mi'kma'ki also includes the Maritimes, parts of <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gasp%C3%A9_Peninsula" title="Gaspé Peninsula">Gaspé Peninsula</a>.) The Mi'kmaq people are among the large Algonquian-language family and inhabited Nova Scotia at the time the first European colonists arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_settlement">European settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: European settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The first Europeans to settle in what is now Nova Scotia were the French, who arrived in 1604, and Catholic Mi'kmaq and Acadians formed the majority of the population of the colony for the next 150 years. In 1605, French colonists established the first permanent European settlement in the future Canada (and the first north of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Florida</a>) at <a href="/wiki/Habitation_at_Port-Royal" class="mw-redirect" title="Habitation at Port-Royal">Port Royal</a>, founding what would become known as <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Morton1999_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morton1999-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Warfare was a notable feature in Nova Scotia during the 17th and 18th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (June 2016)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> During the first 80 years the French and Acadians lived in Nova Scotia, nine significant military clashes took place as the English and Scottish (later British), <a href="/wiki/Jurriaen_Aernoutsz" title="Jurriaen Aernoutsz">Dutch</a> and French fought for possession of the area. These encounters happened at <a href="/wiki/Port_Royal,_Annapolis_County,_Nova_Scotia" title="Port Royal, Annapolis County, Nova Scotia">Port Royal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_New_Brunswick" title="Saint John, New Brunswick">Saint John</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Cap de Sable (present-day <a href="/wiki/Port_La_Tour,_Nova_Scotia" title="Port La Tour, Nova Scotia">Port La Tour, Nova Scotia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jemseg,_New_Brunswick" title="Jemseg, New Brunswick">Jemseg</a> (1674 and 1758) and <a href="/wiki/Baleine,_Nova_Scotia" title="Baleine, Nova Scotia">Baleine</a> (1629). The <a href="/wiki/Acadian_Civil_War" title="Acadian Civil War">Acadian Civil War</a> took place from 1640 to 1645. </p>
      <p>Beginning with <a href="/wiki/King_William%27s_War" title="King William's War">King William's War</a> in 1688, a series of six wars <a href="/wiki/Second_Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Second Hundred Years' War">took place between the English/British and the French</a>, with Nova Scotia being a consistent theatre of conflict between the two powers. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:EvacutionOfPortRoyal1710byCWJefferys.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/EvacutionOfPortRoyal1710byCWJefferys.png/220px-EvacutionOfPortRoyal1710byCWJefferys.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/EvacutionOfPortRoyal1710byCWJefferys.png/330px-EvacutionOfPortRoyal1710byCWJefferys.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/EvacutionOfPortRoyal1710byCWJefferys.png 2x" data-file-width="357" data-file-height="281"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:EvacutionOfPortRoyal1710byCWJefferys.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>French forces withdrawing from <a href="/wiki/Port-Royal_(Acadia)" title="Port-Royal (Acadia)">Port-Royal</a> after being <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Port_Royal_(1710)" title="Siege of Port Royal (1710)">defeated</a> by the British in 1710
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Hostilities between the British and French resumed from 1702 to 1713, known as <a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne%27s_War" title="Queen Anne's War">Queen Anne's War</a>. The British <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Port_Royal_(1710)" title="Siege of Port Royal (1710)">siege of Port Royal</a> took place in 1710, ending French-rule in peninsular Acadia. The subsequent signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> in 1713 formally recognized this, while returning <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a> (<i><i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Île Royale</i></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a> (<i><i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Île Saint-Jean</i></i>) to the French. Despite the British <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Port_Royal_(1710)" title="Siege of Port Royal (1710)">conquest of Acadia</a> in 1710, Nova Scotia remained primarily occupied by Catholic Acadians and Mi'kmaq, who confined British forces to Annapolis and to Canso. Present-day New Brunswick then still formed a part of the French colony of Acadia. Immediately after the capture of Port Royal in 1710, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Nicholson" title="Francis Nicholson">Francis Nicholson</a> announced it would be renamed <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Royal" title="Annapolis Royal">Annapolis Royal</a> in honour of <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne</a>. </p>
      <p>As a result of <a href="/wiki/Father_Rale%27s_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Father Rale's War">Father Rale's War</a> (1722–1725), the Mi'kmaq signed a series of treaties with Great Britain in 1725. The Mi'kmaq signed a treaty of "submission" to the British crown.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> However, conflict between the Acadians, Mi'kmaq, French, and the British persisted in the following decades with <a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_War" title="King George's War">King George's War</a> (1744–1748). </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Father_Le_Loutre%27s_War" title="Father Le Loutre's War">Father Le Loutre's War</a> (1749–1755) began when <a href="/wiki/Edward_Cornwallis" title="Edward Cornwallis">Edward Cornwallis</a> arrived to establish <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax</a> with 13 transports on 21 June 1749.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> A General Court, made up of the governor and the council, was the highest court in the colony at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-nscourts_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nscourts-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Belcher_(jurist)" title="Jonathan Belcher (jurist)">Jonathan Belcher</a> was sworn in as chief justice of the Nova Scotia Supreme Court on 21 October 1754.<sup id="cite_ref-nscourts_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nscourts-26">[26]</a></sup> The first legislative assembly in Halifax, under the Governorship of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lawrence_(British_Army_officer)" title="Charles Lawrence (British Army officer)">Charles Lawrence</a>, met on 2 October 1758.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> of 1754–63 (the North American theatre of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> of 1756–1763), the British <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Acadians" title="Expulsion of the Acadians">deported</a> the Acadians and recruited <a href="/wiki/New_England_Planters" title="New England Planters">New England Planters</a> to resettle the colony. The 75-year period of war ended with the <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Treaties" title="Halifax Treaties">Halifax Treaties</a> between the British and the Mi'kmaq (1761). After the war, some Acadians were allowed to return. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Deportation_Grand-Pr%C3%A9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Deportation_Grand-Pr%C3%A9.jpg/220px-Deportation_Grand-Pr%C3%A9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Deportation_Grand-Pr%C3%A9.jpg/330px-Deportation_Grand-Pr%C3%A9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Deportation_Grand-Pr%C3%A9.jpg/440px-Deportation_Grand-Pr%C3%A9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="753" data-file-height="432"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Deportation_Grand-Pr%C3%A9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Acadians" title="Expulsion of the Acadians">Expulsion of the Acadians</a> in <a href="/wiki/Grand-Pr%C3%A9,_Nova_Scotia" title="Grand-Pré, Nova Scotia">Grand-Pré</a>. More than 80 per cent of the Acadian population was expelled from the region between 1755 and 1764.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1763, most of Acadia (Cape Breton Island, St. John's Island (now <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>), and New Brunswick) became part of Nova Scotia. In 1765, the county of <a href="/wiki/Sunbury_County,_Nova_Scotia" title="Sunbury County, Nova Scotia">Sunbury</a> was created. This included the territory of present-day <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and eastern <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> as far as the <a href="/wiki/Penobscot_River" title="Penobscot River">Penobscot River</a>. In 1769, St. John's Island became a separate colony.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> (1775–1783) had a significant impact on shaping Nova Scotia. Initially, Nova Scotia—"the 14th American Colony" as some called it—displayed ambivalence over whether the colony should join the more southern colonies in their defiance of Britain, and rebellion flared at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Cumberland" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Fort Cumberland">Battle of Fort Cumberland</a> (1776) and at the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Saint_John_(1777)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Saint John (1777)">Siege of Saint John (1777)</a>. Throughout the war, American <a href="/wiki/Privateers" class="mw-redirect" title="Privateers">privateers</a> devastated the maritime economy by capturing ships and looting almost every community outside of Halifax. These American raids alienated many sympathetic or neutral Nova Scotians into supporting the British. By the end of the war Nova Scotia had outfitted a number of privateers to attack American shipping.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> British military forces based at Halifax succeeded in preventing American support for rebels in Nova Scotia and deterred any invasion of Nova Scotia. However the British navy failed to establish naval supremacy. While the British captured many American privateers in battles such as the <a href="/wiki/Naval_battle_off_Halifax" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval battle off Halifax">Naval battle off Halifax</a> (1782), many more continued attacks on shipping and settlements until the final months of the war. The Royal Navy struggled to maintain British supply lines, defending convoys from American and French attacks as in the fiercely fought convoy battle, the <a href="/wiki/Naval_battle_off_Cape_Breton" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval battle off Cape Breton">Naval battle off Cape Breton</a> (1781). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:AricanNovaScotianByCaptain_William_Booth1788.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/AricanNovaScotianByCaptain_William_Booth1788.png/220px-AricanNovaScotianByCaptain_William_Booth1788.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/AricanNovaScotianByCaptain_William_Booth1788.png/330px-AricanNovaScotianByCaptain_William_Booth1788.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/AricanNovaScotianByCaptain_William_Booth1788.png/440px-AricanNovaScotianByCaptain_William_Booth1788.png 2x" data-file-width="622" data-file-height="494"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:AricanNovaScotianByCaptain_William_Booth1788.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Black_Loyalist" title="Black Loyalist">Black Loyalist</a> wood cutter, at <a href="/wiki/Shelburne,_Nova_Scotia" title="Shelburne, Nova Scotia">Shelburne, Nova Scotia</a>, in 1788
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the Thirteen Colonies and their French allies forced the British forces to surrender (1781), approximately 33,000 <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalists</a> (the King's Loyal Americans, allowed to place "<a href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalist" title="United Empire Loyalist">United Empire Loyalist</a>" after their names) settled in Nova Scotia (14,000 of them in what became New Brunswick) on lands granted by the Crown as some compensation for their losses. (The British administration divided Nova Scotia and hived off Cape Breton and <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> in 1784). The Loyalist exodus created new communities across Nova Scotia, including <a href="/wiki/Shelburne,_Nova_Scotia" title="Shelburne, Nova Scotia">Shelburne</a>, which briefly became one of the larger British settlements in North America, and infused Nova Scotia with additional capital and skills. There are also a number of Black loyalists buried in unmarked graves in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Burying_Ground_(Halifax,_Nova_Scotia)" title="Old Burying Ground (Halifax, Nova Scotia)">Old Burying Ground (Halifax, Nova Scotia)</a>. </p>
      <p>However the migration also caused political tensions between Loyalist leaders and the leaders of the existing <a href="/wiki/New_England_Planters" title="New England Planters">New England Planters</a> settlement. The Loyalist influx also pushed Nova Scotia's 2000 Mi'kmaq People to the margins as Loyalist land grants encroached on ill-defined native lands. As part of the Loyalist migration, about 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Black_Loyalist" title="Black Loyalist">Black Loyalists</a> arrived; they founded the largest free Black settlement in North America at <a href="/wiki/Birchtown,_Nova_Scotia" title="Birchtown, Nova Scotia">Birchtown</a>, near Shelburne. Many Nova Scotian communities were <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_in_the_American_Revolution#Loyalist_settlements" title="Nova Scotia in the American Revolution">settled by British regiments that fought in the war</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:John_Christian_Schetky,_H.M.S._Shannon_Leading_Her_Prize_the_American_Frigate_Chesapeake_into_Halifax_Harbour_(c._1830).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/John_Christian_Schetky%2C_H.M.S._Shannon_Leading_Her_Prize_the_American_Frigate_Chesapeake_into_Halifax_Harbour_%28c._1830%29.jpg/220px-John_Christian_Schetky%2C_H.M.S._Shannon_Leading_Her_Prize_the_American_Frigate_Chesapeake_into_Halifax_Harbour_%28c._1830%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/John_Christian_Schetky%2C_H.M.S._Shannon_Leading_Her_Prize_the_American_Frigate_Chesapeake_into_Halifax_Harbour_%28c._1830%29.jpg/330px-John_Christian_Schetky%2C_H.M.S._Shannon_Leading_Her_Prize_the_American_Frigate_Chesapeake_into_Halifax_Harbour_%28c._1830%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/John_Christian_Schetky%2C_H.M.S._Shannon_Leading_Her_Prize_the_American_Frigate_Chesapeake_into_Halifax_Harbour_%28c._1830%29.jpg/440px-John_Christian_Schetky%2C_H.M.S._Shannon_Leading_Her_Prize_the_American_Frigate_Chesapeake_into_Halifax_Harbour_%28c._1830%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1213" data-file-height="863"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:John_Christian_Schetky,_H.M.S._Shannon_Leading_Her_Prize_the_American_Frigate_Chesapeake_into_Halifax_Harbour_(c._1830).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Shannon_(1806)" title="HMS Shannon (1806)">HMS&nbsp;<i>Shannon</i></a> leading the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_USS_Chesapeake" title="Capture of USS Chesapeake">captured</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Chesapeake_(1799)" title="USS Chesapeake (1799)">USS&nbsp;<i>Chesapeake</i></a> into <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a> during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, Nova Scotia's contribution to the British war effort involved communities either purchasing or building various privateer ships to attack U.S. vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Perhaps the most dramatic moment in the war for Nova Scotia occurred when <a href="/wiki/HMS_Shannon_(1806)" title="HMS Shannon (1806)">HMS <i>Shannon</i></a> escorted the captured American frigate <a href="/wiki/USS_Chesapeake_(1799)" title="USS Chesapeake (1799)">USS <i>Chesapeake</i></a> into <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Harbour" title="Halifax Harbour">Halifax Harbour</a> (1813). Many of the U.S. prisoners were kept at <a href="/wiki/Deadman%27s_Island,_Halifax" class="mw-redirect" title="Deadman's Island, Halifax">Deadman's Island, Halifax</a>. </p>
      <p>During this century, Nova Scotia became the first colony in <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> to achieve <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a> in January–February 1848 and become <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing</a> through the efforts of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Howe" title="Joseph Howe">Joseph Howe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Nova Scotia had established <a href="/wiki/Representative_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative government">representative government</a> in 1758, an achievement later commemorated by the erection of the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Sandford_Fleming_Park" title="Sir Sandford Fleming Park">Dingle Tower</a> in 1908. </p>
      <p>Nova Scotians fought in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> of 1853–1856.<sup id="cite_ref-MagocsiOntario1999poiujm_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MagocsiOntario1999poiujm-31">[31]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Welsford-Parker_Monument" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsford-Parker Monument">Welsford-Parker Monument</a> in Halifax is the second-oldest war monument in Canada (1860) and the only Crimean War monument in North America. It commemorates the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1854%E2%80%931855)" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1854–1855)">1854–55 Siege of Sevastopol</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Inauguration_of_the_Welsford-Parker_Monument,_Halifax,_Nova_Scotia,_Canada,_17_July_1860_-_restored.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Inauguration_of_the_Welsford-Parker_Monument%2C_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_17_July_1860_-_restored.jpg/220px-Inauguration_of_the_Welsford-Parker_Monument%2C_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_17_July_1860_-_restored.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Inauguration_of_the_Welsford-Parker_Monument%2C_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_17_July_1860_-_restored.jpg/330px-Inauguration_of_the_Welsford-Parker_Monument%2C_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_17_July_1860_-_restored.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Inauguration_of_the_Welsford-Parker_Monument%2C_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_17_July_1860_-_restored.jpg/440px-Inauguration_of_the_Welsford-Parker_Monument%2C_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada%2C_17_July_1860_-_restored.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3019" data-file-height="2106"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Inauguration_of_the_Welsford-Parker_Monument,_Halifax,_Nova_Scotia,_Canada,_17_July_1860_-_restored.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Inauguration of the <a href="/wiki/Sebastopol_Monument" title="Sebastopol Monument">Sebastopol Monument</a> in 1860. The monument was built to honour Nova Scotians who fought in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Thousands of Nova Scotians fought in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> (1861–1865), primarily on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">North</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Marquis,_Greg_1998_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marquis,_Greg_1998-32">[32]</a></sup> The British Empire (including Nova Scotia) <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/British_proclamation_of_neutrality_in_the_American_Civil_War" class="extiw" title="s:British proclamation of neutrality in the American Civil War">declared itself neutral</a> in the conflict. As a result, Britain (and Nova Scotia) continued to trade with both the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">South</a> and the North. Nova Scotia's economy boomed during the Civil War. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Confederation_history">Post-Confederation history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-Confederation history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Soon after the American Civil War, Pro-Canadian Confederation <a href="/wiki/List_of_premiers_of_Nova_Scotia" title="List of premiers of Nova Scotia">premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Tupper" title="Charles Tupper">Charles Tupper</a> led Nova Scotia into <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a> on 1 July 1867, along with New Brunswick and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Anti-Confederation_Party" title="Anti-Confederation Party">Anti-Confederation Party</a> was led by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Howe" title="Joseph Howe">Joseph Howe</a>. Almost three months later, in the election of 18 September 1867, the Anti-Confederation Party won 18 out of 19 federal seats, and 36 out of 38 seats in the provincial legislature. </p>
      <p>Throughout the 19th century, numerous businesses developed in Nova Scotia became of pan-Canadian and international importance: the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Starr_Manufacturing_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Starr Manufacturing Company (page does not exist)">Starr Manufacturing Company</a> (first skate-manufacturer in Canada), the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Nova_Scotia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of Nova Scotia">Bank of Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cunard_Line" title="Cunard Line">Cunard Line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Keith%27s_Brewery" title="Alexander Keith's Brewery">Alexander Keith's Brewery</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Morse%27s_Tea_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Morse's Tea Company (page does not exist)">Morse's Tea Company</a> (first tea company in Canada), among others. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bluenose_sailing_1921.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Bluenose_sailing_1921.jpg/220px-Bluenose_sailing_1921.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Bluenose_sailing_1921.jpg/330px-Bluenose_sailing_1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Bluenose_sailing_1921.jpg/440px-Bluenose_sailing_1921.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="444"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bluenose_sailing_1921.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <i><a href="/wiki/Bluenose" title="Bluenose">Bluenose</a></i> in 1921. The racing ship became a provincial icon for Nova Scotia in the 1920s and 1930s.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia became a world leader in both building and owning wooden sailing ships in the second half of the 19th century. Nova Scotia produced internationally recognized shipbuilders <a href="/wiki/Donald_McKay" title="Donald McKay">Donald McKay</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Dawson_Lawrence" title="William Dawson Lawrence">William Dawson Lawrence</a>. The fame Nova Scotia achieved from sailors was assured when <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Slocum" title="Joshua Slocum">Joshua Slocum</a> became the first man to sail single-handedly around the world (1895). International attention continued into the following century with the many racing victories of the <i><a href="/wiki/Bluenose" title="Bluenose">Bluenose</a></i> schooner. Nova Scotia was also the birthplace and home of <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Cunard" title="Samuel Cunard">Samuel Cunard</a>, a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a> shipping magnate (born at <a href="/wiki/Halifax_(former_city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Halifax (former city)">Halifax</a>, Nova Scotia) who founded the <a href="/wiki/Cunard_Line" title="Cunard Line">Cunard Line</a>. </p>
      <p>In December 1917, about 2,000 people were killed in the <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Explosion" title="Halifax Explosion">Halifax Explosion</a>. </p>
      <p>In April 2020, <a href="/wiki/2020_Nova_Scotia_attacks" title="2020 Nova Scotia attacks">a killing spree</a> occurred across the province and became the deadliest rampage in Canada's history.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Demographics of Nova Scotia">Demographics of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Canada_Nova_Scotia_Density_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Canada_Nova_Scotia_Density_2016.png/220px-Canada_Nova_Scotia_Density_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Canada_Nova_Scotia_Density_2016.png/330px-Canada_Nova_Scotia_Density_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Canada_Nova_Scotia_Density_2016.png/440px-Canada_Nova_Scotia_Density_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="6115" data-file-height="4921"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Canada_Nova_Scotia_Density_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population density map of Nova Scotia (c. 2016) with county and regional municipality borders shown.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_origins">Ethnic origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ethnic origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>According to the 2006 Canadian census<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> the largest ethnic group in Nova Scotia is <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a> (31.9%), followed by English (31.8%), Irish (21.6%), French (17.9%), German (11.3%), <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">Aboriginal origin</a> (5.3%), <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> (4.1%), <a href="/wiki/Black_Nova_Scotians" title="Black Nova Scotians">Black Canadians</a> (2.8%), <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a> (1.9%) Italian (1.5%), and <a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_peoples" title="North Germanic peoples">Scandinavian</a> (1.4%). 40.9% of respondents identified their ethnicity as "Canadian". </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Maritimer_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritimer English">Maritimer English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Breton English">Cape Breton English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acadian_French" title="Acadian French">Acadian French</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Gaelic" title="Canadian Gaelic">Canadian Gaelic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Canada_2016_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="Canada 2016 Census">2016 Canadian census</a> showed a population of 923,598. Of the 904,285 singular responses to the census question concerning <a href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother tongue">mother tongue</a>, the most commonly reported languages were: </p>
