      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gaidhealtachd-chanadach.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Gaidhealtachd-chanadach.svg/220px-Gaidhealtachd-chanadach.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Gaidhealtachd-chanadach.svg/330px-Gaidhealtachd-chanadach.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Gaidhealtachd-chanadach.svg/440px-Gaidhealtachd-chanadach.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="886" data-file-height="779"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gaidhealtachd-chanadach.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Distribution of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Maritimes" title="The Maritimes">the Maritimes</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia is home to the largest <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>-speaking community outside of Scotland, with a small number of native speakers in <a href="/wiki/Pictou_County" title="Pictou County">Pictou County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antigonish_County" title="Antigonish County">Antigonish County</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a>, and the language is taught in a number of secondary schools throughout the province. In 2018 the government launched a new Gaelic vehicle licence plate to raise awareness of the language and help fund Gaelic language and culture initiatives. They estimated that there were 2,000 Gaelic speakers in the province.<sup id="cite_ref-plate_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plate-36">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1871, the largest religious denominations were Protestant with 103,500 (27%); Roman Catholic with 102,000 (26%); Baptist with 73,295 (19%); Anglican with 55,124 (14%); Methodist with 40,748 (10%), Lutheran with 4,958 (1.3%); and Congregationalist with 2,538 (0.65%).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 2011 census, the largest denominations by number of adherents were Christians with 78.2%. About 21.18% were non-religious and 1% were <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sikhs" title="Sikhs">Sikhs</a> constitute around 0.20%.<sup id="cite_ref-religion2011d_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion2011d-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Nova Scotia's <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_gross_domestic_product" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by gross domestic product">per capita GDP</a> in 2016 was <span style="white-space: nowrap">CA$44,924</span>, significantly lower than the national average per capita GDP of <span style="white-space: nowrap">CA$57,574</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> GDP growth has lagged behind the rest of the country for at least the past decade.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-40">[40]</a></sup> As of 2017, the median family income in Nova Scotia was $85,970, below the national average of $92,990;<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> in Halifax the figure rises to $98,870.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nova_Scotia_DGJ_7889_-_I_can%27t_carry_all_those_lobster_traps!!!!!!!_(4891334833).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Nova_Scotia_DGJ_7889_-_I_can%27t_carry_all_those_lobster_traps%21%21%21%21%21%21%21_%284891334833%29.jpg/220px-Nova_Scotia_DGJ_7889_-_I_can%27t_carry_all_those_lobster_traps%21%21%21%21%21%21%21_%284891334833%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Nova_Scotia_DGJ_7889_-_I_can%27t_carry_all_those_lobster_traps%21%21%21%21%21%21%21_%284891334833%29.jpg/330px-Nova_Scotia_DGJ_7889_-_I_can%27t_carry_all_those_lobster_traps%21%21%21%21%21%21%21_%284891334833%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Nova_Scotia_DGJ_7889_-_I_can%27t_carry_all_those_lobster_traps%21%21%21%21%21%21%21_%284891334833%29.jpg/440px-Nova_Scotia_DGJ_7889_-_I_can%27t_carry_all_those_lobster_traps%21%21%21%21%21%21%21_%284891334833%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nova_Scotia_DGJ_7889_-_I_can%27t_carry_all_those_lobster_traps!!!!!!!_(4891334833).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lobster traps on a dock in <a href="/wiki/Sheet_Harbour,_Nova_Scotia" title="Sheet Harbour, Nova Scotia">Sheet Harbour</a>. The province is the world's largest exporter of lobsters.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The province is the world's largest exporter of <a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">Christmas trees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">lobster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Berry" title="Berry">wild berries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Its export value of fish exceeds $1&nbsp;billion, and fish products are received by 90 countries around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the province's imports far exceed its exports. While these numbers were roughly equal from 1992 until 2004, since that time the trade deficit has ballooned. In 2012, exports from Nova Scotia were 12.1% of provincial GDP, while imports were 22.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia's traditionally <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">resource-based economy</a> has diversified in recent decades. The rise of Nova Scotia as a viable jurisdiction in North America, historically, was driven by the ready availability of natural resources, especially the <a href="/wiki/Fish_stocks" title="Fish stocks">fish stocks</a> off the <a href="/wiki/Scotian_Shelf" title="Scotian Shelf">Scotian Shelf</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishery</a> was a pillar of the economy since its development as part of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> in the 17th century; however, the fishery suffered a sharp decline due to <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a> in the late 20th century. The collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Cod" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Cod">cod stocks</a> and the closure of this sector resulted in a loss of approximately 20,000 jobs in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other sectors in the province were also hit hard, particularly during the last two decades: coal mining in Cape Breton and northern mainland Nova Scotia has virtually ceased, and a <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Steel_Corporation" title="Sydney Steel Corporation">large steel</a> mill in <a href="/wiki/Sydney,_Nova_Scotia" title="Sydney, Nova Scotia">Sydney</a> closed during the 1990s. More recently, the high value of the Canadian dollar relative to the US dollar has hurt the forestry industry, leading to the shutdown of a long-running <a href="/wiki/Bowater_Mersey_Paper_Company_Limited" title="Bowater Mersey Paper Company Limited">pulp and paper mill</a> near <a href="/wiki/Liverpool,_Nova_Scotia" title="Liverpool, Nova Scotia">Liverpool</a>. Mining, especially of <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a> and salt and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Silica" class="mw-redirect" title="Silica">silica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barite" class="mw-redirect" title="Barite">barite</a>, is also a significant sector.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Since 1991, <a href="/wiki/Offshore_drilling" title="Offshore drilling">offshore oil and gas</a> has become an important part of the economy, although production and revenue are now declining.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-40">[40]</a></sup> However, agriculture remains an important sector in the province, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Valley" title="Annapolis Valley">Annapolis Valley</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Grafton,_Nova_Scotia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG/220px-Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG/330px-Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG/440px-Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4912" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Grafton,_Nova_Scotia.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A farm in <a href="/wiki/Grafton,_Nova_Scotia" title="Grafton, Nova Scotia">Grafton</a>. Agriculture remains an important sector of the economy in the <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Valley" title="Annapolis Valley">Annapolis Valley</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia's defence and aerospace sector generates approximately $500&nbsp;million in revenues and contributes about $1.5&nbsp;billion to the provincial economy each year.<sup id="cite_ref-business_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business-48">[48]</a></sup> To date, 40% of Canada's military assets reside in Nova Scotia.<sup id="cite_ref-business_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business-48">[48]</a></sup> Nova Scotia has the fourth-largest <a href="/wiki/Film_industry" title="Film industry">film industry</a> in Canada hosting over 100 productions yearly, more than half of which are the products of international film and television producers.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> In 2015, the government of Nova Scotia eliminated tax credits to film production in the province, jeopardizing the industry given most other jurisdictions continue to offer such credits.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The province also boasts a rapidly developing <a href="/wiki/Information_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Information Technology">Information &amp; Communication Technology</a> (ICT) sector which consists of over 500 companies, and employs roughly 15,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006, the manufacturing sector brought in over $2.6&nbsp;billion in chained GDP, the largest output of any industrial sector in Nova Scotia.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michelin" title="Michelin">Michelin</a> remains by far the largest single employer in this sector, operating three production plants in the province. Michelin is also the province's largest private-sector employer.<sup id="cite_ref-2019nov22michelin_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019nov22michelin-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Nova_Scotia" title="Tourism in Nova Scotia">Tourism in Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Enchantment_of_the_Seas_Halifax_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Enchantment_of_the_Seas_Halifax_2011.jpg/220px-Enchantment_of_the_Seas_Halifax_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Enchantment_of_the_Seas_Halifax_2011.jpg/330px-Enchantment_of_the_Seas_Halifax_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Enchantment_of_the_Seas_Halifax_2011.jpg/440px-Enchantment_of_the_Seas_Halifax_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Enchantment_of_the_Seas_Halifax_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A cruise ship docked at the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Halifax" title="Port of Halifax">Port of Halifax</a>. The port sees more than 200,000 cruise passengers each year.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Nova Scotia tourism industry includes more than 6,500 direct businesses, supporting nearly 40,000 jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Cruise ships pay regular visits to the province. In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Halifax" title="Port of Halifax">Port of Halifax</a> received 261,000 passengers and Sydney 69,000.<sup id="cite_ref-2010indicators_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010indicators-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gov-ns1_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov-ns1-56">[56]</a></sup> This industry contributes approximately $1.3&nbsp;billion annually to the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> A 2008 Nova Scotia tourism campaign included advertising a fictional mobile phone called <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate_(phone)" title="Pomegranate (phone)">Pomegranate</a> and establishing website, which after reading about "new phone" redirected to tourism info about region.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia's tourism industry showcases Nova Scotia's culture, scenery and coastline. Nova Scotia has many museums reflecting its <a href="/wiki/Ethnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic">ethnic</a> heritage, including the <a href="/wiki/Glooscap" title="Glooscap">Glooscap</a> Heritage Centre, <a href="/wiki/Grand-Pr%C3%A9_National_Historic_Site" title="Grand-Pré National Historic Site">Grand-Pré National Historic Site</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hector_(ship)" title="Hector (ship)">Hector Heritage Quay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Cultural_Centre_for_Nova_Scotia" title="Black Cultural Centre for Nova Scotia">Black Cultural Centre for Nova Scotia</a>. Other museums tell the story of its working history, such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Breton_Miners%27_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cape Breton Miners' Museum (page does not exist)">Cape Breton Miners' Museum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic" title="Maritime Museum of the Atlantic">Maritime Museum of the Atlantic</a>. </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia is home to several internationally renowned musicians and there are visitor centres in the home towns of <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rita_MacNeil" title="Rita MacNeil">Rita MacNeil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">Anne Murray</a> Centre. There are also numerous music and cultural festivals such as the <a href="/wiki/Stan_Rogers_Folk_Festival" title="Stan Rogers Folk Festival">Stan Rogers Folk Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Colours" title="Celtic Colours">Celtic Colours</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Gaelic_Mod" title="Nova Scotia Gaelic Mod">Nova Scotia Gaelic Mod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Nova_Scotia_International_Tattoo" title="Royal Nova Scotia International Tattoo">Royal Nova Scotia International Tattoo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Film_Festival" title="Atlantic Film Festival">Atlantic Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Fringe_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Fringe Festival">Atlantic Fringe Festival</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lighthouse_DSC01066_-_Peggy%27s_Cove_Lighthouse_(7612052968).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lighthouse_DSC01066_-_Peggy%27s_Cove_Lighthouse_%287612052968%29.jpg/220px-Lighthouse_DSC01066_-_Peggy%27s_Cove_Lighthouse_%287612052968%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lighthouse_DSC01066_-_Peggy%27s_Cove_Lighthouse_%287612052968%29.jpg/330px-Lighthouse_DSC01066_-_Peggy%27s_Cove_Lighthouse_%287612052968%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lighthouse_DSC01066_-_Peggy%27s_Cove_Lighthouse_%287612052968%29.jpg/440px-Lighthouse_DSC01066_-_Peggy%27s_Cove_Lighthouse_%287612052968%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6035" data-file-height="4053"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lighthouse_DSC01066_-_Peggy%27s_Cove_Lighthouse_(7612052968).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Peggys_Point_Lighthouse" title="Peggys Point Lighthouse">Peggys Point Lighthouse</a> in <a href="/wiki/Peggys_Cove,_Nova_Scotia" class="mw-redirect" title="Peggys Cove, Nova Scotia">Peggys Cove</a> is a tourist attraction in the province.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The province has <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Historic_Sites_of_Canada_in_Nova_Scotia" title="List of National Historic Sites of Canada in Nova Scotia">87 National Historic Sites of Canada</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Habitation_at_Port-Royal" class="mw-redirect" title="Habitation at Port-Royal">Habitation at Port-Royal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Louisbourg" title="Fortress of Louisbourg">Fortress of Louisbourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citadel_Hill_(Fort_George)" title="Citadel Hill (Fort George)">Citadel Hill (Fort George)</a> in Halifax. Nova Scotia has two national parks, <a href="/wiki/Kejimkujik_National_Park" title="Kejimkujik National Park">Kejimkujik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Highlands_National_Park" title="Cape Breton Highlands National Park">Cape Breton Highlands</a>, and many other <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Nova_Scotia" title="List of protected areas of Nova Scotia">protected areas</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a> has the highest tidal range in the world, and the iconic <a href="/wiki/Peggys_Cove,_Nova_Scotia" class="mw-redirect" title="Peggys Cove, Nova Scotia">Peggys Cove</a> is internationally recognized and receives 600,000-plus visitors a year.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lunenburg,_Nova_Scotia" title="Lunenburg, Nova Scotia">Old Town Lunenburg</a> is a port town on the South Shore that was declared a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>. </p>
      <p>Acadian Skies and Mi'kmaq Lands is a starlight reserve in southwestern Nova Scotia. It is the first certified <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>-Starlight Tourist Destination. Starlight tourist destinations are locations that offer conditions for observations of stars which are protected from light pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Government of Nova Scotia">Government of Nova Scotia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Politics of Nova Scotia">Politics of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia is ordered by a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary government</a> within the construct of <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_in_Nova_Scotia" title="Monarchy in Nova Scotia">monarchy in Nova Scotia</a> is the foundation of the executive, <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial</a> branches.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The sovereign is <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, who also serves as head of state of <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">15 other Commonwealth countries</a>, each of Canada's nine other provinces, and the Canadian federal realm, and resides predominantly in the United Kingdom. As such, the Queen's representative, the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Lieutenant Governor of Nova Scotia">Lieutenant Governor of Nova Scotia</a> (at present <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Joseph_LeBlanc" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur Joseph LeBlanc">Arthur Joseph LeBlanc</a>), carries out most of the royal duties in Nova Scotia. </p>
      <p>The direct participation of the royal and viceroyal figures in any of these areas of governance is limited, though; in practice, their use of the executive powers is directed by <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Executive Council of Nova Scotia">the Executive Council</a>, a committee of <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Crown" title="Minister of the Crown">ministers of the Crown</a> responsible to the unicameral, elected <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_House_of_Assembly" title="Nova Scotia House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a> and chosen and headed by the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Premier of Nova Scotia">Premier of Nova Scotia</a> (presently <a href="/wiki/Iain_Rankin" class="mw-redirect" title="Iain Rankin">Iain Rankin</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. To ensure the stability of government, the lieutenant governor will usually appoint as premier the person who is the current leader of the political party that can obtain the confidence of a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a> in the House of Assembly. The leader of the party with the second-most seats usually becomes the <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Nova Scotia)">Leader of Her Majesty's Loyal Opposition</a> (presently <a href="/wiki/Tim_Houston" title="Tim Houston">Tim Houston</a>) and is part of an adversarial parliamentary system intended to keep the government in check.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Each of the 51 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Legislative_Assembly" title="Member of the Legislative Assembly">Members of the Legislative Assembly</a> in the House of Assembly is elected by single member plurality in an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district_(Canada)" title="Electoral district (Canada)">electoral district</a> or riding. General elections must be called by the lieutenant governor on the advice of the premier, or may be triggered by the government losing a <a href="/wiki/Confidence_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Confidence vote">confidence vote</a> in the House.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> There are three dominant political parties in Nova Scotia: the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Liberal_Party" title="Nova Scotia Liberal Party">Liberal Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_New_Democratic_Party" title="Nova Scotia New Democratic Party">New Democratic Party</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Association_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Progressive Conservative Association of Nova Scotia">Progressive Conservative Party</a>. The other two registered parties are the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Green Party of Nova Scotia">Green Party of Nova Scotia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantica_Party" title="Atlantica Party">Atlantica Party</a>, neither of which has a seat in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly" title="House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a>. </p>
      <p>The province's revenue comes mainly from the taxation of personal and corporate income, although taxes on tobacco and alcohol, its stake in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Lottery_Corporation" title="Atlantic Lottery Corporation">Atlantic Lottery Corporation</a>, and oil and gas royalties are also significant. In 2006–07, the province passed a budget of $6.9&nbsp;billion, with a projected $72&nbsp;million surplus. Federal equalization payments account for $1.385&nbsp;billion, or 20.07% of the provincial revenue. The province participates in the <a href="/wiki/Harmonized_Sales_Tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Harmonized Sales Tax">HST</a>, a blended sales tax collected by the federal government using the <a href="/wiki/Goods_and_Services_Tax_(Canada)" class="mw-redirect" title="Goods and Services Tax (Canada)">GST</a> tax system. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_of_Nova_Scotia" title="List of counties of Nova Scotia">List of counties of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nova_Scotia_counties_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="Map showing locations of Nova Scotia's historical counties" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Nova_Scotia_counties_2015.png/250px-Nova_Scotia_counties_2015.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Nova_Scotia_counties_2015.png/375px-Nova_Scotia_counties_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Nova_Scotia_counties_2015.png/500px-Nova_Scotia_counties_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="3400" data-file-height="2921"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nova_Scotia_counties_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Distribution of Nova Scotia's 18 historical counties by <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Nova_Scotia" title="List of municipalities in Nova Scotia">municipal status</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Unlike the provinces of <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, which have two-tiered municipality systems, Nova Scotia has a one-tier system of municipalities<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> inclusive of four municipality types – <a href="/wiki/Regional_municipality#Nova_Scotia" title="Regional municipality">regional municipalities</a>, towns, <a href="/wiki/County#Canada" title="County">county municipalities</a> and <a href="/wiki/District_municipality#Usage_in_Nova_Scotia" title="District municipality">district municipalities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2015MuniStats_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015MuniStats-66">[66]</a></sup> Regional municipalities may incorporate under the <i>Municipal Government Act</i> (<i>MGA</i>) of 1998, which came into force on 1 April 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-history_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-67">[67]</a></sup> while towns, county municipalities and district municipalities are continued as municipalities under the <i>MGA</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MGA_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MGA-68">[68]</a></sup> The <i>MGA</i> gives municipal councils the power to make bylaws for "health, well being, safety and protection of persons" and "safety and protection of property" in addition to a few expressed powers.<sup id="cite_ref-FCM_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCM-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Of its 50 municipalities, Nova Scotia has three regional municipalities, 26 towns, nine county municipalities and 12 district municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-2015MuniStats_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015MuniStats-66">[66]</a></sup> The regional municipality of <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax</a> is the capital and largest municipality of Nova Scotia by population with 403,131 residents representing <span data-sort-value="7001436478857684836?" style="display:none"></span>44% of the total population of the province and land area at 5,490.35&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (2,119.84&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-2016StatCanNS_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016StatCanNS-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pictou" title="Pictou">Pictou</a> was the first municipality to incorporate <span data-sort-value="000000001874-05-04-0000" style="white-space:nowrap">4 May 1874</span>, and the newest municipalities are Halifax and <a href="/wiki/Region_of_Queens_Municipality,_Nova_Scotia" class="mw-redirect" title="Region of Queens Municipality, Nova Scotia">Region of Queens Municipality</a> both amalgamating into their present regional municipality form of government <span data-sort-value="000000001996-04-01-0000" style="white-space:nowrap">1 April 1996</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-incorporations_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incorporations-71">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture<span class="anchor" id="Culture"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine" title="Cuisine">cuisine</a> of Nova Scotia is typically <a href="/wiki/Canadian_cuisine" title="Canadian cuisine">Canadian</a> with an emphasis on local seafood. One endemic dish (in the sense of "peculiar to" and "originating from") is the <a href="/wiki/Donair" class="mw-redirect" title="Donair">Halifax donair</a>, a distant variant of the <a href="/wiki/Doner_kebab" title="Doner kebab">doner kebab</a> prepared using thinly sliced beef <a href="/wiki/Meatloaf" title="Meatloaf">meatloaf</a> and a sweet <a href="/wiki/Condensed_milk" title="Condensed milk">condensed milk</a> sauce. As well, <a href="/wiki/Hodge-Podge_(soup)" title="Hodge-Podge (soup)">hodge podge</a>, a creamy soup of fresh baby vegetables, is native to Nova Scotia.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The province is also known for a dessert called blueberry <a href="/wiki/Dumpling" title="Dumpling">grunt.</a><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_and_festivals">Events and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Events and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are a number of <a href="/wiki/Festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Festivals">festivals</a> and cultural events that are recurring in Nova Scotia, or notable in its history. The following is an incomplete list of festivals and other cultural gatherings in the province: </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television">Film and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Film and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Nova Scotia has produced numerous film actors. <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominee <a href="/wiki/Elliot_Page" title="Elliot Page">Elliot Page</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Juno_(film)" title="Juno (film)">Juno</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i>) was born in Halifax, Nova Scotia; five-time <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominee <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Kennedy" title="Arthur Kennedy">Arthur Kennedy</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Arabia_(film)" title="Lawrence of Arabia (film)">Lawrence of Arabia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/High_Sierra_(film)" title="High Sierra (film)">High Sierra</a></i>) called Nova Scotia his home; and two time <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Donald_Sutherland" title="Donald Sutherland">Donald Sutherland</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/MASH_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="MASH (film)">MASH</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ordinary_People" title="Ordinary People">Ordinary People</a></i>) spent most of his youth in the province. Other actors include <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Tremblay" title="John Paul Tremblay">John Paul Tremblay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robb_Wells" title="Robb Wells">Robb Wells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Smith_(actor)" title="Mike Smith (actor)">Mike Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Dunsworth" title="John Dunsworth">John Dunsworth</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Trailer_Park_Boys" title="Trailer Park Boys">Trailer Park Boys</a></i> and actress <a href="/wiki/Joanne_Kelly" title="Joanne Kelly">Joanne Kelly</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Warehouse_13" title="Warehouse 13">Warehouse 13</a></i>. </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia has also produced numerous film directors such as <a href="/wiki/Thom_Fitzgerald" title="Thom Fitzgerald">Thom Fitzgerald</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Hanging_Garden_(film)" title="The Hanging Garden (film)">The Hanging Garden</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Petrie" title="Daniel Petrie">Daniel Petrie</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Resurrection_(1980_film)" title="Resurrection (1980 film)">Resurrection</a></i>—Academy Award nominee) and Acadian film director <a href="/wiki/Phil_Comeau" title="Phil Comeau">Phil Comeau</a>'s multiple award-winning local story (<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Le_secret_de_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Le secret de Jérôme (film) (page does not exist)">Le secret de Jérôme</a></i>). </p>
      <p>Nova Scotian stories are the subject of numerous feature films: <i><a href="/wiki/Margaret%27s_Museum" title="Margaret's Museum">Margaret's Museum</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Helena_Bonham_Carter" title="Helena Bonham Carter">Helena Bonham Carter</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bay_Boy" title="The Bay Boy">The Bay Boy</a></i> (directed by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Petrie" title="Daniel Petrie">Daniel Petrie</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Kiefer_Sutherland" title="Kiefer Sutherland">Kiefer Sutherland</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/New_Waterford_Girl" title="New Waterford Girl">New Waterford Girl</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Adele_H." title="The Story of Adele H.">The Story of Adele H.</a></i> (the story of unrequited love of <a href="/wiki/Ad%C3%A8le_Hugo" title="Adèle Hugo">Adèle Hugo</a>); and two films of <i>Evangeline</i> (one starring <a href="/wiki/Miriam_Cooper" title="Miriam Cooper">Miriam Cooper</a> and another starring <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del Río">Dolores del Río</a>). </p>
      <p>There is a significant film industry in Nova Scotia. Feature filmmaking began in Canada with <i>Evangeline</i> (1913), made by <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Bioscope_Company" title="Canadian Bioscope Company">Canadian Bioscope Company</a> in Halifax, which released six films before it closed. The film has since been lost. Some of the award-winning feature films made in the province are <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kate_Winslet" title="Kate Winslet">Kate Winslet</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shipping_News" title="The Shipping News">The Shipping News</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Spacey" title="Kevin Spacey">Kevin Spacey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julianne_Moore" title="Julianne Moore">Julianne Moore</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/K-19:_The_Widowmaker" title="K-19: The Widowmaker">K-19: The Widowmaker</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Ford" title="Harrison Ford">Harrison Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liam_Neeson" title="Liam Neeson">Liam Neeson</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/Amelia_(film)" title="Amelia (film)">Amelia</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Hilary_Swank" title="Hilary Swank">Hilary Swank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Gere" title="Richard Gere">Richard Gere</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ewan_McGregor" title="Ewan McGregor">Ewan McGregor</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lighthouse_(2019_film)" title="The Lighthouse (2019 film)">The Lighthouse</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Robert_Pattinson" title="Robert Pattinson">Robert Pattinson</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Dafoe" class="mw-redirect" title="William Dafoe">William Dafoe</a>). </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia has also produced numerous television series: <i><a href="/wiki/This_Hour_Has_22_Minutes" title="This Hour Has 22 Minutes">This Hour Has 22 Minutes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Messer%27s_Jubilee" title="Don Messer's Jubilee">Don Messer's Jubilee</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Harbour" title="Black Harbour">Black Harbour</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Haven_(TV_series)" title="Haven (TV series)">Haven</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Trailer_Park_Boys" title="Trailer Park Boys">Trailer Park Boys</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._D" title="Mr. D">Mr. D</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Call_Me_Fitz" title="Call Me Fitz">Call Me Fitz</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Theodore_Tugboat" title="Theodore Tugboat">Theodore Tugboat</a></i>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Jesse_Stone_(character)" title="Jesse Stone (character)">Jesse Stone</a></i> film series on <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> starring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Selleck" title="Tom Selleck">Tom Selleck</a> is also routinely produced in the province. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_arts">Fine arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Fine arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia.JPG/220px-Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia.JPG/330px-Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia.JPG/440px-Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Art Gallery of Nova Scotia">Art Gallery of Nova Scotia</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Provincial_museums_of_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Provincial museums of Canada">provincial art gallery</a> of Nova Scotia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia has long been a centre for artistic and cultural excellence. The capital, Halifax, hosts institutions such as <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_College_of_Art_and_Design_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Scotia College of Art and Design University">Nova Scotia College of Art and Design University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Art Gallery of Nova Scotia">Art Gallery of Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neptune_Theatre_(Halifax)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neptune Theatre (Halifax)">Neptune Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_Arts_Centre" title="Dalhousie Arts Centre">Dalhousie Arts Centre</a>, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Two_Planks_and_a_Passion_Theatre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Two Planks and a Passion Theatre (page does not exist)">Two Planks and a Passion Theatre</a>. The province is home to avant-garde visual art and traditional crafting, writing and publishing and a film industry. </p>
      <p>Much of the historic public art sculptures in the province were made by New York sculptor <a href="/wiki/J._Massey_Rhind" title="J. Massey Rhind">J. Massey Rhind</a> as well as Canadian sculptors <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_MacCarthy" title="Hamilton MacCarthy">Hamilton MacCarthy</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_William_Hill_(sculptor)" title="George William Hill (sculptor)">George Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Hahn" title="Emanuel Hahn">Emanuel Hahn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis-Philippe_H%C3%A9bert" title="Louis-Philippe Hébert">Louis-Philippe Hébert</a>. Some of this public art was also created by Nova Scotian <a href="/wiki/John_Wilson_(sculptor)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Wilson (sculptor)">John Wilson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Nova Scotian <a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Lang_(builder)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="George Lang (builder) (page does not exist)">George Lang</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Stone_sculpture" title="Stone sculpture">stone sculptor</a> who also built many landmark buildings in the province, including the <a href="/wiki/Welsford-Parker_Monument" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsford-Parker Monument">Welsford-Parker Monument</a>. Two valuable sculptures/ monuments in the province are in <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Church_(Halifax)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Paul's Church (Halifax)">St. Paul's Church (Halifax)</a>: one by <a href="/wiki/John_Gibson_(sculptor)" title="John Gibson (sculptor)">John Gibson</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Richard_John_Uniacke,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Richard John Uniacke, Jr.">Richard John Uniacke, Jr.</a>) and another monument by Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Leggatt_Chantrey" title="Francis Leggatt Chantrey">Francis Leggatt Chantrey</a> (for Amelia Ann Smyth). Both Gibson and Chantry were famous British sculptors during the Victorian era and have numerou sculptures in the <a href="/wiki/Tate" title="Tate">Tate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Fine_Arts,_Boston" title="Museum of Fine Arts, Boston">Museum of Fine Arts, Boston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>. </p>
      <p>Some of the province's greatest painters were <a href="/wiki/Maud_Lewis" title="Maud Lewis">Maud Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Valentine_(painter)" title="William Valentine (painter)">William Valentine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Frances_Ann_Morris" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Frances Ann Morris">Maria Morris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_L._Gray" title="Jack L. Gray">Jack L. Gray</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mabel_Killiam_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mabel Killiam Day (page does not exist)">Mabel Killiam Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Lawson" title="Ernest Lawson">Ernest Lawson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frances_Bannerman" title="Frances Bannerman">Frances Bannerman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Colville" title="Alex Colville">Alex Colville</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tom_Forrestall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tom Forrestall (page does not exist)">Tom Forrestall</a> and ship portrait artist <a href="/wiki/John_O%27Brien_(marine_artist)" title="John O'Brien (marine artist)">John O'Brien</a>. Some of most notable artists whose works have been acquired by Nova Scotia are British artist <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Reynolds" title="Joshua Reynolds">Joshua Reynolds</a> (collection of Art Gallery of Nova Scotia); <a href="/wiki/William_Gush" title="William Gush">William Gush</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_J._Weaver" title="William J. Weaver">William J. Weaver</a> (both have works in <a href="/wiki/Province_House_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Province House (Nova Scotia)">Province House</a>); <a href="/wiki/Robert_Field_(painter)" title="Robert Field (painter)">Robert Field</a> (<a href="/wiki/Government_House_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Government House (Nova Scotia)">Government House</a>), as well as leading American artists <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_West" title="Benjamin West">Benjamin West</a> (self portrait in <a href="/wiki/The_Halifax_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="The Halifax Club">The Halifax Club</a>, portrait of chief justice in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Supreme_Court" title="Nova Scotia Supreme Court">Nova Scotia Supreme Court</a>), <a href="/wiki/John_Singleton_Copley" title="John Singleton Copley">John Singleton Copley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Feke" title="Robert Feke">Robert Feke</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Field_(painter)" title="Robert Field (painter)">Robert Field</a> (the latter three have works in the <a href="/wiki/Richard_John_Uniacke" title="Richard John Uniacke">Uniacke Estate</a>). Two famous Nova Scotian photographers are <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wallace_R._MacAskill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wallace R. MacAskill (page does not exist)">Wallace R. MacAskill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Hines" title="Sherman Hines">Sherman Hines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Three of the most accomplished illustrators were <a href="/wiki/George_Wylie_Hutchinson" title="George Wylie Hutchinson">George Wylie Hutchinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Chambers_(cartoonist)" title="Bob Chambers (cartoonist)">Bob Chambers (cartoonist)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donald_A._Mackay" title="Donald A. Mackay">Donald A. Mackay</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are numerous Nova Scotian authors who have achieved international fame: <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Chandler_Haliburton" title="Thomas Chandler Haliburton">Thomas Chandler Haliburton</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sam_Slick" title="Sam Slick">The Clockmaker</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Alistair_MacLeod" title="Alistair MacLeod">Alistair MacLeod</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/No_Great_Mischief" title="No Great Mischief">No Great Mischief</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_M._Richardson" title="Evelyn M. Richardson">Evelyn Richardson</a> <i>(We Keep A Light)</i>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Marshall_Saunders" title="Margaret Marshall Saunders">Margaret Marshall Saunders</a> <i>(<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Joe" title="Beautiful Joe">Beautiful Joe</a>),</i> <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Bradford_Dakin" title="Laurence Bradford Dakin">Laurence B. Dakin</a> <i>(Marco Polo),</i> and <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Slocum" title="Joshua Slocum">Joshua Slocum</a> <i>(<a href="/wiki/Sailing_Alone_Around_the_World" title="Sailing Alone Around the World">Sailing Alone Around the World</a>).</i> Other authors include <a href="/wiki/Johanna_Skibsrud" title="Johanna Skibsrud">Johanna Skibsrud</a> <i>(The Sentimentalists),</i> <a href="/wiki/Alden_Nowlan" title="Alden Nowlan">Alden Nowlan</a> <i>(Bread, Wine and Salt),</i> <a href="/wiki/George_Elliott_Clarke" title="George Elliott Clarke">George Elliott Clarke</a> <i>(Execution Poems),</i> <a href="/wiki/Lesley_Choyce" title="Lesley Choyce">Lesley Choyce</a> <i>(Nova Scotia: Shaped by the Sea),</i> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Raddall" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Raddall">Thomas Raddall</a> <i>(Halifax: Warden of the North),</i> <a href="/wiki/Donna_Morrissey" title="Donna Morrissey">Donna Morrissey</a> <i>(Kit's Law),</i> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Parker_Day" title="Frank Parker Day">Frank Parker Day</a> <i>(<a href="/wiki/Rockbound" title="Rockbound">Rockbound</a>).</i> </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia has also been the subject of numerous literary books. Some of the international best-sellers are: <i>Last Man Out: The Story of the Springhill Mining Disaster</i> (by <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Fay_Greene" title="Melissa Fay Greene">Melissa Fay Greene</a>)&nbsp;; <i>Curse of the Narrows: The <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Explosion" title="Halifax Explosion">Halifax Explosion</a> 1917</i> (by Laura MacDonald); "In the Village" (short story by <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>–winning author <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Bishop" title="Elizabeth Bishop">Elizabeth Bishop</a>); and <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Critics_Circle_Award" title="National Book Critics Circle Award">National Book Critics Circle Award</a> winner <i><a href="/wiki/Rough_Crossings" title="Rough Crossings">Rough Crossings</a></i> (by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Schama" title="Simon Schama">Simon Schama</a>). Other authors who have written novels about Nova Scotian stories include: <a href="/wiki/Linden_MacIntyre" title="Linden MacIntyre">Linden MacIntyre</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Bishop%27s_Man" title="The Bishop's Man">The Bishop's Man</a></i>); <a href="/wiki/Hugh_MacLennan" title="Hugh MacLennan">Hugh MacLennan</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Barometer_Rising" title="Barometer Rising">Barometer Rising</a></i>); <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Buckler" title="Ernest Buckler">Ernest Buckler</a> (<i>The Valley and the Mountain</i>); <a href="/wiki/Archibald_MacMechan" title="Archibald MacMechan">Archibald MacMechan</a> (<i>Red Snow on Grand Pré</i>), <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wadsworth_Longfellow" title="Henry Wadsworth Longfellow">Henry Wadsworth Longfellow</a> (long poem <i><a href="/wiki/Evangeline" title="Evangeline">Evangeline</a></i>); <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Hill" title="Lawrence Hill">Lawrence Hill</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Negroes_(novel)" title="The Book of Negroes (novel)">The Book of Negroes</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/John_Mack_Faragher" title="John Mack Faragher">John Mack Faragher</a> (<i>Great and Nobel Scheme</i>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Music of Nova Scotia">Music of Nova Scotia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Symphony_Nova_Scotia_performs_at_the_Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Symphony_Nova_Scotia_performs_at_the_Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic.jpg/220px-Symphony_Nova_Scotia_performs_at_the_Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Symphony_Nova_Scotia_performs_at_the_Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic.jpg/330px-Symphony_Nova_Scotia_performs_at_the_Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Symphony_Nova_Scotia_performs_at_the_Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic.jpg/440px-Symphony_Nova_Scotia_performs_at_the_Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="496"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Symphony_Nova_Scotia_performs_at_the_Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Symphony_Nova_Scotia" title="Symphony Nova Scotia">Symphony Nova Scotia</a> performing at the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic" title="Maritime Museum of the Atlantic">Maritime Museum of the Atlantic</a> in Halifax
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nova Scotia is home to <a href="/wiki/Symphony_Nova_Scotia" title="Symphony Nova Scotia">Symphony Nova Scotia</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Symphony_orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Symphony orchestra">symphony orchestra</a> based in Halifax. The province has produced more than its fair share of famous musicians, including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Denny_Doherty" title="Denny Doherty">Denny Doherty</a> (from <a href="/wiki/The_Mamas_%26_the_Papas" title="The Mamas &amp; the Papas">The Mamas &amp; the Papas</a>), <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">Anne Murray</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sarah_McLachlan" title="Sarah McLachlan">Sarah McLachlan</a>, country singers <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Canyon" title="George Canyon">George Canyon, and Drake Jensen</a>, jazz vocalist <a href="/wiki/Holly_Cole" title="Holly Cole">Holly Cole</a>, classical performers <a href="/wiki/Portia_White" title="Portia White">Portia White</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Hannigan" title="Barbara Hannigan">Barbara Hannigan</a>, multi <a href="/wiki/Juno_Award" title="Juno Award">Juno Award</a> nominated rapper <a href="/wiki/Classified_(rapper)" title="Classified (rapper)">Classified</a>, and such diverse artists as <a href="/wiki/Rita_MacNeil" title="Rita MacNeil">Rita MacNeil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Mays" title="Matt Mays">Matt Mays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sloan_(band)" title="Sloan (band)">Sloan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feist_(singer)" title="Feist (singer)">Feist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Todd_Fancey" title="Todd Fancey">Todd Fancey</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Rankin_Family" title="The Rankin Family">The Rankin Family</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalie_MacMaster" title="Natalie MacMaster">Natalie MacMaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Crowe" title="Susan Crowe">Susan Crowe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buck_65" title="Buck 65">Buck 65</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joel_Plaskett" title="Joel Plaskett">Joel Plaskett</a>, and the bands <a href="/wiki/April_Wine" title="April Wine">April Wine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grand_D%C3%A9rangement_(band)" title="Grand Dérangement (band)">Grand Dérangement</a> </p>
      <p>There are numerous songs written about Nova Scotia: The Ballad of Springhill (written by <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Seeger" title="Peggy Seeger">Peggy Seeger</a> and performed by Irish folk singer <a href="/wiki/Luke_Kelly" title="Luke Kelly">Luke Kelly</a>, a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Dubliners" title="The Dubliners">The Dubliners</a>); several songs by <a href="/wiki/Stan_Rogers" title="Stan Rogers">Stan Rogers</a> including Bluenose, Watching The Apples Grow, The Jeannie C (mentions Little Dover, NS), <a href="/wiki/Barrett%27s_Privateers" title="Barrett's Privateers">Barrett's Privateers</a>, Giant, and The Rawdon Hills; Farewell to Nova Scotia (traditional); Blue Nose (<a href="/wiki/Stompin%27_Tom_Connors" title="Stompin' Tom Connors">Stompin' Tom Connors</a>); She's Called Nova Scotia (by <a href="/wiki/Rita_MacNeil" title="Rita MacNeil">Rita MacNeil</a>); Cape Breton (by <a href="/wiki/David_Myles_(singer-songwriter)" class="mw-redirect" title="David Myles (singer-songwriter)">David Myles</a>); <a href="/wiki/Acadian_Driftwood" title="Acadian Driftwood">Acadian Driftwood</a> (by <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Robertson" title="Robbie Robertson">Robbie Robertson</a>); Acadie (by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Lanois" title="Daniel Lanois">Daniel Lanois</a>); <a href="/wiki/Song_for_the_Mira" class="mw-redirect" title="Song for the Mira">Song For The Mira</a> (by <a href="/wiki/Allister_MacGillivray" title="Allister MacGillivray">Allister MacGillivray</a>) and My Nova Scotia Home (by <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow</a>). </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia has produced many significant songwriters, such as <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winning <a href="/wiki/Gordie_Sampson" title="Gordie Sampson">Gordie Sampson</a>, who has written songs for <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood" title="Carrie Underwood">Carrie Underwood</a> ("Jesus, Take the Wheel", "Just a Dream", "Get Out of This Town"), <a href="/wiki/Martina_McBride" title="Martina McBride">Martina McBride</a> ("If I Had Your Name", "You're Not Leavin Me"), <a href="/wiki/LeAnn_Rimes" title="LeAnn Rimes">LeAnn Rimes</a> ("Long Night", "Save Myself"), and <a href="/wiki/George_Canyon" title="George Canyon">George Canyon</a> ("My Name"). Many of <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow's</a> songs went on to be recorded by the likes of <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash" title="Johnny Cash">Johnny Cash</a>. Cape Bretoners <a href="/wiki/Allister_MacGillivray" title="Allister MacGillivray">Allister MacGillivray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leon_Dubinsky" title="Leon Dubinsky">Leon Dubinsky</a> have both written songs which, by being covered by so many popular artists, and by entering the repertoire of so many choirs around the world, have become iconic representations of Nova Scotian style, values and ethos. Dubinsky's pop ballad "<a href="/wiki/Rise_Again_(The_Rankin_Family_song)" title="Rise Again (The Rankin Family song)">We Rise Again</a>" might be called the unofficial anthem of Cape Breton.<sup id="cite_ref-Leon_Dubinsky_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leon_Dubinsky-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Music producer <a href="/wiki/Brian_Ahern_(producer)" title="Brian Ahern (producer)">Brian Ahern</a> is a Nova Scotian. He got his start by being music director for CBC television's <a href="/wiki/Singalong_Jubilee" title="Singalong Jubilee">Singalong Jubilee</a>. He later produced 12 albums for <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">Anne Murray</a> ("Snowbird", "Danny's Song" and "You Won't See Me"); 11 albums for <a href="/wiki/Emmylou_Harris" title="Emmylou Harris">Emmylou Harris</a> (whom he married at his home in Halifax on 9 January 1977).<sup id="cite_ref-Brian_Ahern_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brian_Ahern-77">[77]</a></sup> He also produced discs for <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash" title="Johnny Cash">Johnny Cash</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Jones" title="George Jones">George Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Orbison" title="Roy Orbison">Roy Orbison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glen_Campbell" title="Glen Campbell">Glen Campbell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Williams" title="Don Williams">Don Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Winchester" title="Jesse Winchester">Jesse Winchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linda_Ronstadt" title="Linda Ronstadt">Linda Ronstadt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ahern_Allmusic_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ahern_Allmusic-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Grammy winning songwriter and music producer <a href="/wiki/Cirkut" title="Cirkut">Cirkut</a>, known for writing and producing songs for <a href="/wiki/The_Weeknd" title="The Weeknd">The Weeknd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>, was born and raised in Halifax before moving to Toronto in 2004. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles_at_Halifax_Mooseheads_(February_6_2010)_(4336519788).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles_at_Halifax_Mooseheads_%28February_6_2010%29_%284336519788%29.jpg/220px-Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles_at_Halifax_Mooseheads_%28February_6_2010%29_%284336519788%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles_at_Halifax_Mooseheads_%28February_6_2010%29_%284336519788%29.jpg/330px-Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles_at_Halifax_Mooseheads_%28February_6_2010%29_%284336519788%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles_at_Halifax_Mooseheads_%28February_6_2010%29_%284336519788%29.jpg/440px-Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles_at_Halifax_Mooseheads_%28February_6_2010%29_%284336519788%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles_at_Halifax_Mooseheads_(February_6_2010)_(4336519788).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> game between the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Breton Screaming Eagles">Cape Breton Screaming Eagles</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Mooseheads" title="Halifax Mooseheads">Halifax Mooseheads</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Major_Junior" class="mw-redirect" title="Major Junior">Major Junior</a> hockey teams in Nova Scotia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sport is an important part of Nova Scotia culture. There are numerous semi pro, university and amateur sports teams, for example, The <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Mooseheads" title="Halifax Mooseheads">Halifax Mooseheads</a>, 2013 Canadian Hockey League Memorial Cup Champions, and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Breton Screaming Eagles">Cape Breton Screaming Eagles</a>, both of the Quebec Major Junior Hockey League. The <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Hurricanes" title="Halifax Hurricanes">Halifax Hurricanes</a> of the National Basketball League of Canada is another team that calls Nova Scotia home, and were 2016 league champions.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Professional soccer came to the province in 2019 in the form of <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Premier_League" title="Canadian Premier League">Canadian Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/HFX_Wanderers_FC" title="HFX Wanderers FC">HFX Wanderers FC</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Open" title="Nova Scotia Open">Nova Scotia Open</a> was a professional <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> tournament on the <a href="/wiki/Web.com_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="Web.com Tour">Web.com Tour</a> in 2014 and 2015. </p>
      <p>The province has also produced numerous athletes such as <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Crosby" title="Sidney Crosby">Sidney Crosby</a> (ice hockey), <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Mackinnon" class="mw-redirect" title="Nathan Mackinnon">Nathan Mackinnon</a> (ice hockey), <a href="/wiki/Brad_Marchand" title="Brad Marchand">Brad Marchand</a> (ice hockey), <a href="/wiki/Colleen_Jones" title="Colleen Jones">Colleen Jones</a> (curling), <a href="/wiki/Al_MacInnis" title="Al MacInnis">Al MacInnis</a> (ice hockey), <a href="/wiki/TJ_Grant" title="TJ Grant">TJ Grant</a> (mixed martial arts), <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Johnson" title="Rocky Johnson">Rocky Johnson</a> (wrestling, and father of <a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Johnson" title="Dwayne Johnson">Dwayne "The Rock" Johnson</a>), <a href="/wiki/George_Dixon_(boxer)" title="George Dixon (boxer)">George Dixon</a> (boxing) and <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Johnson" title="Kirk Johnson">Kirk Johnson</a> (boxing). The achievements of Nova Scotian athletes are presented at the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Sport_Hall_of_Fame" title="Nova Scotia Sport Hall of Fame">Nova Scotia Sport Hall of Fame</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SteAnnes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/SteAnnes.jpg/220px-SteAnnes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/SteAnnes.jpg/330px-SteAnnes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/SteAnnes.jpg/440px-SteAnnes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1414" data-file-height="1185"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SteAnnes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Sainte-Anne" title="Université Sainte-Anne">Université Sainte-Anne</a> is a Francophone university situated in <a href="/wiki/Pointe-de-l%27%C3%89glise,_Nova_Scotia" title="Pointe-de-l'Église, Nova Scotia">Pointe-de-l'Église</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Minister of Education is responsible for the administration and delivery of education, as defined by the Education Act<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> and other acts relating to colleges, universities and private schools. The powers of the Minister and the Department of Education are defined by the Ministerial regulations and constrained by the Governor-In-Council regulations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>All children until the age of 16 are legally required to attend school or the parent needs to perform home schooling.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Nova Scotia's education system is split up into eight different regions including; Tri-County (22 schools), Annapolis Valley (42 schools), South Shore (25 schools), Chignecto-Central (67 schools), Halifax (135 schools), Strait (20 schools) and Cape Breton-Victoria Regional Centre for Education (39 schools).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nova Scotia has more than 450 public schools for children. The public system offers primary to Grade 12. There are also private schools in the province. Public education is administered by seven regional school boards, responsible primarily for English instruction and French immersion, and also province-wide by the <a href="/wiki/Conseil_Scolaire_Acadien_Provincial" class="mw-redirect" title="Conseil Scolaire Acadien Provincial">Conseil Scolaire Acadien Provincial</a>, which administers French instruction to students whose primary language is French.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Community_College" title="Nova Scotia Community College">Nova Scotia Community College</a> system has 13 campuses around the province. With a focus on training and education, the <a href="/wiki/College_(Canada)" title="College (Canada)">college</a> was established in 1988 by amalgamating the province's former vocational schools. In addition to the provincial community college system, there are more than 90 registered private colleges in Nova Scotia.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ten universities are also situated in Nova Scotia, including <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_University" title="Dalhousie University">Dalhousie University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_King%27s_College" title="University of King's College">University of King's College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Mary%27s_University_(Halifax)" title="Saint Mary's University (Halifax)">Saint Mary's University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Saint_Vincent_University" title="Mount Saint Vincent University">Mount Saint Vincent University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_College_of_Art_and_Design" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Scotia College of Art and Design">NSCAD University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acadia_University" title="Acadia University">Acadia University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Sainte-Anne" title="Université Sainte-Anne">Université Sainte-Anne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Francis_Xavier_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Francis Xavier University">Saint Francis Xavier University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_University" title="Cape Breton University">Cape Breton University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_School_of_Theology" title="Atlantic School of Theology">Atlantic School of Theology</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
